2:26:1683:0:14:72:348:700:12:Times:12:Times:Minimum Wages and the Distribution of Family Incomes
2:27:1735:14:14:72:148:686:12:Times:12:Times:Arindrajit Dube
2:28:1750:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 25240
2:29:1778:14:14:72:150:658:12:Times:12:Times:November 2018
2:30:1791:14:28:72:203:644:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. I32,I38,J2,J38,J58
2:31:1817:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:32:1825:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:There  is  robust  evidence  that  higher  minimum  wages  increase  family  incomes  at  the  bottom  of 
2:33:1931:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:the distribution.  The  long  run  (3  or  more  years)  minimum  wage  elasticity  of  the  non-elderly 
2:34:2035:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:poverty  rate with  respect  to  the  minimum  wage  ranges  between  -0.220  and  -0.459  across 
2:35:2132:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:alternative  specifications. The  long  run  minimum  wage  elasticities  for  the  10th  and  15th 
2:36:2231:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:unconditional   quantiles   of   family   income range   between   0.152   and   0.430   depending   on 
2:37:2334:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:specification.  A  reduction  in  public  assistance  partly offsets  these  income  gains,  which  are  on 
2:38:2441:14:14:72:542:504:12:Times:12:Times:average  66%  as  large  when  using  an  expanded  income  definition including  tax  credits  and  non-
2:39:2545:14:42:72:141:490:12:Times:12:Times:cash transfers.
2:40:2560:42:14:72:148:448:12:Times:12:Times:Arindrajit Dube
2:41:2575:14:14:72:198:434:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics
2:42:2598:14:14:72:208:420:12:Times:12:Times:University of Massachusetts
2:43:2625:14:14:72:126:406:12:Times:12:Times:Crotty Hall
2:44:2636:14:14:72:179:392:12:Times:12:Times:412 N. Pleasant Street
2:45:2658:14:14:72:172:378:12:Times:12:Times:Amherst, MA 01002
2:46:2675:14:14:72:124:364:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
2:47:2683:14:0:72:192:350:12:Times:12:Times:adube@econs.umass.edu
3:48:2704:0:33:72:185:709:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:1  Introduction
3:49:2719:33:22:71:540:676:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:At least since Gramlich (1976), economists have recognized that the ability of minimum wage policy
3:50:2817:22:22:71:539:654:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to aid lower-income families depends on the joint distribution of wage gains, potential job losses, and
3:51:2920:22:22:71:539:632:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:other sources of family income. The poverty-reducing effects of the minimum wage is expected to be
3:52:3018:22:22:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:small if job losses from a minimum wage increase are sizable, or if most minimum wage workers are
3:53:3115:22:22:72:542:588:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:higher up in the family income distribution—say because they are teens from higher income families,
3:54:3214:22:22:72:540:566:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:or because their spouses are paid well. Therefore, the extent to which minimum wages raise family
3:55:3311:22:22:72:535:544:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:incomes at the bottom of the distribution is not cleara priori, and has to be studied empirically.
3:56:3409:22:22:88:539:522:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:However, while there is a large and active literature on the employment effects of minimum
3:57:3499:22:21:71:540:500:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages—see Belman and Wolfson (2014) for a recent review—there are relatively fewer studies that
3:58:3594:21:22:72:540:479:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:empirically estimate the impact of the policy on family incomes. Compounding the problem, the
3:59:3687:22:22:72:540:457:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:existing papers often suffer from a number of key shortcomings including insufficient attention to
3:60:3785:22:22:72:540:435:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the validity of the research design, and use of small samples sometimes with limited minimum wage
3:61:3882:22:22:71:465:413:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:variation—all of which tend to produce somewhat erratic and imprecise estimates.
3:62:3962:22:22:88:540:391:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In this paper, I use individual-level data from the March Current Population Survey (CPS)
3:63:4051:22:22:72:540:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:between 1984 and 2013 to provide a more complete assessment of how U.S. minimum wage policies
3:64:4144:22:22:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:shift the distribution of family incomes for the non-elderly population than has been to date.1This
3:65:4243:22:22:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:paper makes three important advances over the existing literature. First, I fully characterize how
3:66:4341:22:22:72:540:303:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:minimum wage increases shift the cumulative distribution of family incomes, and subsequently use
3:67:4437:22:22:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:this to estimate unconditional quantile partial effects (UQPE) of the policy. This provides a fuller
3:68:4537:22:22:72:540:259:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:picture of the distributional effects of the policy than available to date. Second, I show how the
3:69:4635:22:22:72:540:237:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income effects by quantile varies when we consider broader income definitions to include tax credits
3:70:4735:22:21:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and non-cash transfers. I am able to quantify the extent to which offsets through reduced public
3:71:4831:21:22:72:540:194:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:assistance affects the distributional impact of minimum wages. Third, I provide estimates that are
3:72:4929:22:22:72:540:172:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:more credibly causal than in the literature by utilizing a wide range of specifications with alternative
3:73:5033:22:22:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:sets of controls for time-varying heterogeneity, and by assessing the assumption of parallel trends
3:74:5132:22:22:72:540:128:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:using an array of falsification tests across the income distribution. Specifically, I use distributed lag
3:75:5237:22:20:72:540:106:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:specifications that both includes leads and up to three years of lags in the minimum wage, allowing
3:76:5336:20:14:87:541:86:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:1In this paper, when I refer to the 1984-2013 period, I am referring to the survey years for the March CPS. Note,
3:77:5449:14:0:72:498:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:however, that respondents in March 2013 CPS survey are asked about their income during the year 2012.
4:78:5551:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for a delayed impact of the policy; and I allow for time varying heterogeneity by region, business
4:79:5649:22:22:72:222:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cycles and state-specific trends.
4:80:5682:22:22:88:539:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Overall, I find robust evidence that higher minimum wages lead to increases in incomes at the
4:81:5775:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:bottom of the family income distribution. For the poverty rate, long-run minimum wage elasticities
4:82:5873:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:between -0.220 and -0.459 obtain from eight specifications ranging from the classic two-way fixed
4:83:5970:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effects model to a model with a rich set of controls for trends, regional shocks and business cycle
4:84:6069:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:heterogeneity. All of these estimates are statistically distinguishable from zero at conventional
4:85:6166:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:levels.2There is a reduction in the shares below income cutoffs between 50 and 125 percent of the
4:86:6263:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:federal poverty threshold (FPT), with the largest proportionate reductions occurring around 75
4:87:6357:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:percent of the poverty threshold (elasticities ranging between -0.186 and -0.566). When I look across
4:88:6458:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:demographic groups using the preferred (most saturated) specification, the poverty rate elasticities
4:89:6558:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:are similar when restricted to younger (under 30) and lower credentialed individuals without a
4:90:6652:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:high school degree. However, the elasticity is relatively larger for black and Latino individuals
4:91:6749:21:22:70:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(-0.872), while relatively smaller for single mothers (-0.327). The poverty reducing effects are not
4:92:6849:22:22:72:519:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:substantially different after 1996, in the period following welfare reform and EITC expansion.
4:93:6943:22:22:88:539:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:By estimating how a minimum wage increase affects the shares of population with incomes
4:94:7030:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:below various multiples of the federal poverty threshold we identify the effect of the policy on the
4:95:7130:22:22:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the cumulative distribution function (CDF) of equivalized family incomes. Subsequently, we can
4:96:7224:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:invert the impact of the policy on the CDF to estimate the impact on an income quantile, i.e., the
4:97:7322:22:22:72:542:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:UQPE. I use the recentered influence function (RIF) regression approach of Firpo et al. (2009),
4:98:7417:22:22:71:539:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:which performs this inversion using a local linear approximation to the counterfactual CDF. This
4:99:7513:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:local inversion entails rescaling the marginal effect of minimum wages on the share above an income
4:100:7612:22:30:72:350:226:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:cutoff by the probability density of income at that cutoff.3
4:101:7672:30:15:87:539:196:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:2Most results in this paper are for the non-elderly population; so when I refer to “the poverty rate,” I am referring
4:102:7789:15:11:72:540:181:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:to the poverty rate among those under 65 years of age. Also, as a matter of terminology, in this paper virtually all
4:103:7905:11:11:72:540:170:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:elasticities are elasticities with respect to the minimum wage. For brevity, I will sometimes refer to “the elasticity of
4:104:8026:11:11:72:540:159:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the poverty rate with respect to the minimum wage” as either “the minimum wage elasticity for the poverty rate” or
4:105:8140:11:11:72:540:148:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:simply “the poverty rate elasticity.” The same is true for elasticities of other outcomes with respect to the minimum
4:106:8257:11:7:71:420:137:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:wage, such as family income quantiles, the proportion under one-half poverty line, etc.
4:107:8344:7:15:87:539:130:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:3It is useful to contrast the UQPE with estimates from the more familiar (conditional) quantile regression. The
4:108:8455:15:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:quantile regression provides us with an estimate of the the impact of minimum wages on, say, the 10th conditional
4:109:8568:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:quantile of family incomes.  This tells us how the policy affects those with unusually low income within their
4:110:8678:11:11:72:541:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:demographic group, e.g., a college graduate with an income that is lowrelativeto others in her educational category.
4:111:8794:11:10:72:541:82:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:However, here we are interested in the effect of the policy on those with low incomes in anabsolute(or unconditional)
4:112:8911:10:0:72:456:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:sense, while controlling for covariates such as education. This is exactly what UQPE measures.
5:113:9006:0:22:88:539:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:I find clear, positive effects of minimum wages on family incomes below the 20th quantile. The
5:114:9100:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:largest impact occurs at the 10th and 15th quantiles, where estimates from most specifications
5:115:9194:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:are statistically significant, and the long run minimum wage elasticities for these family income
5:116:9291:22:22:72:541:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quantiles range between 0.152 and 0.430 depending on control sets. In the preferred (most saturated)
5:117:9391:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:specification, the family income elasticities with respect to the minimum wage are around 0.359 and
5:118:9490:22:22:72:542:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:0.332 for the 10th and 15th quantiles, respectively, and diminish close to zero by the 30th quantile.
5:119:9591:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Since the conventional income definition used for official poverty calculations does not include tax
5:120:9691:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credits such as the Earned Income Tax Credit (EITC), or non-cash transfers such as Supplemental
5:121:9786:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Nutritional Assistance Program (SNAP), I also estimate the impact using an expanded income
5:122:9876:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:definition. After accounting for tax credits and non-cash transfers, the minimum wage effect on
5:123:9971:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the level of family incomes (i.e., the semi-elasticities) are about 66% as large for the bottom 30
5:124:10069:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:percent of the distribution. Overall, the evidence clearly points to at least moderate income gains
5:125:10168:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for low income families resulting from minimum wage increases. At the same time, there is evidence
5:126:10266:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for some substitution of government transfers with earnings as evidenced by the somewhat smaller
5:127:10362:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income increase accounting for tax credit and non-cash transfers such as SNAP and EITC. The
5:128:10453:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:estimates are similar from the more recent period (e.g., post 1996) when the policy environment is
5:129:10551:22:22:72:386:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:more homogeneous following welfare reform and EITC expansion.
5:130:10612:22:22:88:541:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:While this paper substantially improves upon existing research on the topic of minimum wages,
5:131:10705:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:family income distribution and poverty, the existing research is consistent with the proposition
5:132:10801:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that minimum wages likely reduce poverty. In online Appendix A, I quantitatively assess estimates
5:133:10898:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:from the 13 key papers in the literature by collecting or constructing nearly every minimum wage
5:134:10994:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:elasticity for the poverty rate from those studies for a variety of demographic groups. 72 out of the
5:135:11095:22:22:71:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:78 elasticities have a negative sign, and a simple average of the 78 elasticities produces a poverty
5:136:11195:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rate elasticity of -0.18, while the average of the median elasticities from each study is -0.17. For
5:137:11295:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:8 of the 13 studies that actually report an estimate for overall poverty (as opposed to narrower
5:138:11391:22:21:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:subgroups), the average of poverty rate elasticities is -0.13. These averages are broadly consistent
5:139:11491:21:22:71:539:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with the range of findings in this paper in pointing toward a poverty reduction effect of minimum
5:140:11588:22:22:71:406:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages, though they tend to be smaller in magnitude than what I find.
5:141:11656:22:22:88:541:95:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:At the same time, the existing evidence is clouded by serious shortcomings in these studies:
5:142:11748:22:0:72:540:73:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:insufficient controls for state-level heterogeneity; short time periods, sometimes with little minimum
6:143:11851:0:22:71:539:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wage variation; over-statement of precision due to improper methods of statistical inference; and the
6:144:11952:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:use of idiosyncratic sets of outcomes and target groups. In contrast, I use 30 years of data from a
6:145:12051:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:period with a large amount of cross-state minimum wage variation. I also pay close attention to the
6:146:12150:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:non-random nature of minimum wage policies (Allegretto et al. 2017). Since there is disagreement
6:147:12246:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the literature on the appropriateness of particular specifications, I show results using eight
6:148:12343:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:different specifications with alternative controls for state-level heterogeneity that subsumes much
6:149:12442:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the approaches used in the literature. Starting with the classic two-way fixed effects model, I
6:150:12540:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:progressively add regional controls, state specific trends, and state-specific business cycle effects—all
6:151:12645:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of which have been shown to be important in the extant minimum wage literature (e.g., Allegretto
6:152:12741:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:et al. 2017, Zipperer 2016). The resulting set of estimates produces a credible range regardless
6:153:12837:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of one’s priors on, say, the desirability of using regional controls. At the same time, I assess the
6:154:12937:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:internal validity of various specifications using a host of falsification tests including estimating effects
6:155:13045:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:higher up in the income distribution, as well as analyzing leading effects (pre-existing trends) across
6:156:13148:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:specifications. I show that the inclusion of controls for such state-level heterogeneity tends both to
6:157:13250:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:improve performance on falsification tests and to increase the magnitude of the estimated elasticity
6:158:13350:22:22:72:320:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the poverty rate with respect to minimum wages.
6:159:13400:22:22:88:539:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This paper adds to a growing literature that estimates distributional effects of policies using
6:160:13495:22:22:71:539:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a quasi-experimental design. For example, Havnes and Mogstad (2015) also use RIF regressions
6:161:13587:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in a difference-in-difference setting to study the distributional impact of universal child care and
6:162:13687:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:find that a small average effect masks the more sizable increases in adult earnings at the bottom
6:163:13784:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quantiles. The distributional analysis in this paper is also similar to Hoynes and Patel (2016), who
6:164:13884:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:show how EITC expansion shifted the lower end of the family income distribution. Finally, Autor
6:165:13979:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:et al. (2016) estimate the effect of minimum wages on the hourly wage distribution, refining the
6:166:14075:22:22:72:215:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:earlier analysis by Lee (1999).
6:167:14106:22:22:88:539:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The rest of the paper is structured as follows. In section 2, I describe the data and research
6:168:14200:22:21:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:design, including the RIF estimation of unconditional quantile partial effects. Section 3 presents my
6:169:14301:21:22:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:empirical findings on the effect of minimum wages on the proportions below various low-income
6:170:14394:22:0:72:542:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cutoffs as well as on income quantiles. Section 4 concludes with a discussion of the policy implications.
7:171:14500:0:34:72:274:709:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:2  Data and research design
7:172:14527:34:29:72:279:675:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:2.1  Data and sample construction
7:173:14560:29:22:72:541:646:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:I use individual level data from the UNICON extract of the March Current Population Survey (CPS)
7:174:14656:22:22:72:539:624:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:between 1984 and 2013. I augment the CPS data with information on state EITC supplements,4
7:175:14746:22:22:72:540:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:state per-capita GDP, and state unemployment rates from the University of Kentucky Center for
7:176:14839:22:21:72:540:580:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Poverty Research, and state and federal minimum wages from the U.S. Department of Labor. I take
7:177:14934:21:22:72:540:559:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the average of the effective minimum wage (maximum of the state or federal minimums) during
7:178:15025:22:22:72:540:537:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the year for which respondents report incomes. For example, I match the the effective monthly
7:179:15118:22:22:72:540:515:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:minimum wage averaged over January through December of 2011 in a given state to respondents
7:180:15209:22:22:72:263:493:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:from that state in the 2012 March CPS.
7:181:15247:22:22:88:541:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:There is extensive variation in minimum wages over the 30 year period studied in this paper.
7:182:15339:22:22:72:540:449:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Figure B.1 plots the nominal federal minimum wage, as well as the 50th, 75th and 90th percentiles
7:183:15436:22:22:72:540:427:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the effective nominal minimum wages (weighted by population). As the figure shows, the effective
7:184:15535:22:22:72:540:405:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:minimum wage varied substantially over this period across different states. It is also the case that
7:185:15635:22:22:72:540:383:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:there has been much more variation in minimum wages since 2000. Therefore, the inclusion of more
7:186:15731:22:22:72:542:361:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:recent data is particularly helpful as it allows us to estimate the effects of the policy more precisely.
7:187:15836:22:22:88:539:339:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The primary goal of this paper is to characterize how minimum wage changes affect the entire
7:188:15928:22:22:72:540:317:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:distribution of family incomes; for this reason, most of the analysis is performed for the non-elderly
7:189:16030:22:21:72:539:295:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:population as a whole.5The exclusion of the elderly is motivated by the fact that they have much
7:190:16126:21:22:72:540:274:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:lower rates of poverty than the rest of the population, in large part due to Social Security. For
7:191:16223:22:22:72:540:252:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:example, CPS data from March 2013 shows that 9.1 percent (2.7 percent) of the elderly had incomes
7:192:16320:22:22:72:540:230:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:under the poverty line (one-half the poverty line), whereas the corresponding proportions for the
7:193:16417:22:22:72:540:208:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:non-elderly population were 15.9 and 7.2 percent, respectively. For this reason, we are unlikely to
7:194:16516:22:22:72:540:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:learn very much about the impact of minimum wages on the bottom quantiles of the family income
7:195:16610:22:22:72:540:164:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:distribution from studying the elderly. Finally, a focus on the non-elderly is also common in the
7:196:16707:22:34:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:literature (e.g., Burkhauser and Sabia 2007, Sabia and Nielsen 2015). However, I also show that the
7:197:16806:34:15:87:539:108:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:4Many states specify a percentage of the federal EITC as a supplement to be paid to state taxpayers. I use this
7:198:16917:15:7:72:333:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:state EITC supplement rate in my analysis as a control variable.
7:199:16981:7:14:87:539:86:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:5Official poverty measures do not include unrelated individuals under 15 years of age; for this reason I exclude
7:200:17093:14:0:72:193:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:them from the sample as well.
8:201:17123:0:22:72:409:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:overall estimates are quite similar if we include the elderly population.
8:202:17196:22:22:88:539:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:As I discuss in Online Appendix A, a number of researchers have studied the impact of minimum
8:203:17289:22:22:71:539:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages on children and single mothers (e.g., Morgan and Kickham 2001, DeFina 2008, Gundersen
8:204:17380:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and Ziliak 2004).  Several studies have also considered younger adults, or adults with limited
8:205:17474:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:education; these include Neumark (2016), Addison and Blackburn (1999), and Sabia and Nielsen
8:206:17566:22:22:70:539:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(2015). Besides estimating the effect of minimum wages on the incomes of the non-elderly population
8:207:17665:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:overall, I also show key results by demographic groups similar to those that have been studied in
8:208:17762:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the literature. These include (1) all individuals without a high school degree (3) individuals younger
8:209:17864:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:than 30 without a high school degree, (4) individuals with high school or less schooling, (5) black
8:210:17963:22:22:72:541:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:or Latino individuals, (6) children under 18 years of age, (7) all adults and (8) single (unmarried)
8:211:18063:22:38:72:180:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:mothers with children.
8:212:18085:38:28:72:281:451:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:2.2  Outcomes and research design
8:213:18118:28:22:71:540:423:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This paper focuses on equivalized6real family income, defined as multiples of the federal poverty
8:214:18215:22:22:72:541:401:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:threshold:yit=YitFPT(Ni,Childreni,t). This is also sometimes referred to as the income-to-needs (ITN)
8:215:18316:22:22:72:540:379:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:ratio. As is standard,yitis the ratio between family income,Yit, and the federal poverty threshold
8:216:18414:22:22:72:540:357:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:FPT(Ni,Childreni,t)—which depends on family size (Ni) and the number of children, and varies
8:217:18506:22:22:72:540:335:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:by year (t). I start with the conventional definition of family income as is used for official poverty
8:218:18608:22:22:72:540:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:measurement: pre-tax cash income which includes earnings and cash transfers, but does not include
8:219:18705:22:22:72:539:291:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:non-cash benefits or tax credits.7I use the term family to refer to primary families, sub-families, as
8:220:18807:22:22:71:540:269:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:well as single (non-family) householders. Family income and poverty thresholds are computed for
8:221:18902:22:22:72:208:247:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:each family type separately.8
8:222:18931:22:22:88:541:225:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The official poverty measure excludes non-cash transfers such as SNAP and housing assistance,
8:223:19024:22:22:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:as well as tax credits such as EITC. As Fox et al. (2014) shows, exclusion of these categories of
8:224:19121:22:22:72:540:181:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income tends to understate the economic gains made by families in the lower end of the income
8:225:19214:22:18:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:distribution during the 1990s and 2000s. Moreover, there is evidence that minimum wages may
8:226:19305:18:11:87:375:141:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:6Equivalized family income is adjusted for family size and composition.
8:227:19376:11:15:87:541:130:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:7Eligible income includes earnings (excluding capital loss or gains), unemployment compensation, workers’
8:228:19481:15:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:compensation, Social Security, Supplemental Security Income, cash-based public assistance such as Temporary
8:229:19588:11:11:71:541:104:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:Assistance to Needy Families (TANF), veterans’ payments, survivor benefits, pension or retirement income, interest,
8:230:19703:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:dividends, rents, royalties, income from estates, trusts, educational assistance, alimony, child support, assistance from
8:231:19824:11:7:72:358:82:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:outside the household, and other miscellaneous sources of cash income.
8:232:19894:7:0:87:378:75:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:8I use the FAMINC and POVCUT variables from the UNICON extract.
9:233:19958:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:reduce some types of transfers such as SNAP (Reich and West 2015). Therefore, I also show income
9:234:20054:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quantile elasticities using an expanded income definition that includes monetized value of non-cash
9:235:20153:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:transfers (SNAP, housing assistance, school lunch) and refundable tax credits (EITC, child tax
9:236:20247:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:credit, and additional child tax credit). The values for the non-cash transfers are self reported, while
9:237:20351:22:37:72:513:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tax credits are calculated by the Census Bureau based on the respondents’ reported income.
9:238:20441:37:29:72:450:584:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f14:Poverty rate and shares under multiples of federal poverty threshold
9:239:20509:29:22:71:539:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To estimate the impact of minimum wages on the share with income underctimes the federal
9:240:20597:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:poverty threshold, I use a linear probability model where the dependent variable is an indicator for
9:241:20697:22:22:71:539:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:whether individualiis in a family whose equivalized incomeyitfalls belowc:Icit=1(yit< c). As
9:242:20789:22:22:72:432:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:an example, the share withI1it= 1corresponds to the official poverty rate.
9:243:20863:22:22:88:541:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A distributed lag version of the classic two-way (state and time) fixed effects regression specifi-
9:244:20962:22:44:72:164:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cation is as follows:
9:245:20983:44:0:144:170:401:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f11:Icit=
9:246:20988:0:25:182:191:414:8:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f15:3∑
9:247:20990:25:0:173:195:389:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f13:k=−1
9:248:20994:0:32:197:540:401:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:αckln(MWs(i)t−k) +XitΛc+Ws(i)tΨc+μcs(i)+θct+-cit(1)
9:249:21045:32:22:88:540:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Hereμcs(i)is the state fixed effect,θctis the time fixed effect, and-citis the regression error
9:250:21140:22:22:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:term. The regression coefficients and the error components are all indexed bycto clarify that they
9:251:21238:22:22:72:539:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:are from separate regressions for each cutoffcas a multiple of the federal poverty threshold. The
9:252:21335:22:22:72:539:303:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:coefficientαLRc=αc0+αc1+αc2+αc3is the long run semi-elasticity of the proportion under the
9:253:21425:22:22:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income-to-needs cutoff,c, with respect to the minimum wage,MWs(i)t,indexed by the state of
9:254:21515:22:22:72:542:259:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:residences(i)of individualiand timet. The coefficientαMRc=αc0+αc1+αc2is the “medium run”
9:255:21603:22:22:72:540:237:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:semi-elasticity inclusive of the effect up to two years after the policy change. These are converted
9:256:21703:22:22:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to elasticities by dividing by the sample mean of the population share below the cutoff,F(c). For
9:257:21800:22:21:72:539:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:example,βLRc=1F(c)×(αc0+αc1+αc2+αc3)is the long run elasticity. The explicit inclusion
9:258:21886:21:22:72:540:172:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the lagged treatment variable may be of particular relevance when the specification includes a
9:259:21983:22:22:72:542:150:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:state-specific linear trend. With state trends, but without lagged treatment included as a regressor,
9:260:22084:22:22:72:540:128:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a delayed impact can lead to a mis-estimation of the state trends, attenuating the measured effect
9:261:22182:22:22:72:540:106:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the treatment (e.g., Wolfers 2006, Meer and West 2015). Explicit inclusion of up to 3 years of
9:262:22279:22:0:72:297:84:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:lags in minimum wages mitigates this problem.
10:263:22325:0:22:88:539:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The inclusion of a leading minimum wage term allows us to net out any level differences in the
10:264:22419:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:outcome between treated and control states just prior to treatment. As a consequence, the medium
10:265:22515:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and long run elasticities do not reflect such differences, unlike in a static model. Additionally, the
10:266:22617:22:22:70:539:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:“leading value”(βc,−1)provides us with a falsification test to discern the reliability of a research
10:267:22717:22:22:71:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:design. A statistically significant or sizable leading value,βc,−1, indicates that the specification
10:268:22817:22:22:72:542:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:may not be able to account for a violation of the parallel trends assumption prior to treatment,
10:269:22913:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and hence may provide misleading estimates.9To clarify, theβτ,−1term in not included inβMRcor
10:270:23006:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:βLRc.At the same time, aβτ,−16= 0indicates that the treated and control units had some deviation
10:271:23102:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in trends in the past, which raises questions about whether there may be additional deviations in
10:272:23199:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:trends in the future. For this reason, I subject all the specifications to the leading value falsification
10:273:23305:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:test, and use this information as a criteria for model selection. In some cases, I also show the
10:274:23401:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cumulative response with 3 years of leads and 3 years of lags in minimum wages to better evaluate
10:275:23498:22:21:72:432:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the assumption of parallel trends right before the minimum wage increases.
10:276:23572:21:22:88:541:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:All regressions control for individual-level covariatesXit(quartic in age, and dummies for gender,
10:277:23670:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:race and ethnicity, education, family size, number of own children, and marital status), as well as
10:278:23769:22:22:72:542:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:state-level covariatesWs(i)t(unemployment rate, state EITC supplement, and per capita GDP).
10:279:23860:22:22:71:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We can calculate the minimum wage elasticity for the proportion underc,γc, by dividingαcby
10:280:23950:22:22:72:539:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the sample proportion underc. Therefore,γ1corresponds to the elasticity of the poverty rate
10:281:24041:22:22:71:539:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with respect to the minimum wage. The state-level unemployment rate and per-capita GDP are
10:282:24131:22:22:71:539:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:time-varying controls to account for aggregate economic shocks in the state that are unlikely to
10:283:24227:22:22:71:539:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:be affected by the policy, given the small share of minimum wage workers in the workforce. All
10:284:24321:22:22:72:542:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:regressions and summary statistics in this paper are weighted by the March CPS sample weights.
10:285:24415:22:22:72:462:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Finally, the standard errors are clustered by state, which is the unit of treatment.
10:286:24499:22:22:88:539:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A problem with the two-way fixed effects model is that there are many potential time varying
10:287:24591:22:22:72:542:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:confounders when it comes to the distribution of family incomes. As shown in Allegretto et al.
10:288:24685:22:21:70:539:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(2013), high- versus low-minimum wage states over this period are highly spatially clustered, and
10:289:24782:21:22:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tend to differ in terms of growth in income inequality and job polarization, and the severity of
10:290:24878:22:31:72:540:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:business cycles. To account for such confounders, I also estimate specifications that allow for
10:291:24973:31:14:87:539:86:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:9For example, Dube et al. (2010) and Allegretto et al. (2017) show that the two-way fixed effects model often fails
10:292:25088:14:0:72:470:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:this falsification test when it comes to minimum wage impact on teen and restaurant employment.
11:293:25184:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:arbitrary regional shocks by the nine Census divisions, by incorporating division-specific year effects
11:294:25287:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:θcd(i)t. This is motivated by the finding in Allegretto et al. (2011) and Dube et al. (2010) of the
11:295:25386:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:importance of spatial heterogeneity in estimating minimum wage effects on employment, and these
11:296:25481:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:papers utilize division-specific time effects as well. Additionally, I will consider specifications with
11:297:25585:22:22:72:502:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:state-specific linear trends,σs(i)t, to account for long run trend differences between states.
11:298:25679:22:22:88:539:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Given the importance of the business cycle as a determinant of family incomes and movements
11:299:25770:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the poverty rate, I pay special attention to the issue in this paper. The inclusion of the state
11:300:25869:22:22:72:542:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:unemployment rate and year dummies are the usual means of accounting for cyclical factors.
11:301:25959:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:However, there are strong prior reasons to worry about business cycle heterogeneity across states
11:302:26056:22:22:71:539:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:when it comes to poverty and minimum wages. Allegretto et al. (2013) show that minimum wage
11:303:26147:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:increases are not uniformly distributed throughout the business cycle—they tend to occur more
11:304:26240:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:frequently during the second half of economic expansions. That paper also shows that states with
11:305:26336:22:21:72:542:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:higher minimum wages over the 1990-2012 period experienced sharper business cycle fluctuations.
11:306:26431:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Moreover, states with higher minimum wages may systematically differ with respect to other
11:307:26521:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:attributes (such as unemployment insurance generosity) which may affect how a given change in the
11:308:26618:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:state unemployment rate translates into changes in family incomes or the incidence of poverty. As
11:309:26715:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:another illustration, Zipperer (2016) shows that low wage employment was much more reliant on
11:310:26808:22:22:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the construction sectors in states bound by the federal minimum wage increase during 2007-2009; as
11:311:26906:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a result, these states suffered a much steeper relative decline in low wage employment during this
11:312:27004:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:period quite independent of minimum wage policy. For these reasons, I also consider specifications
11:313:27102:22:22:72:539:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that include state-specific Great-Recession-year indicators,ρcr(t)s(i), whereby a dummy for each
11:314:27198:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Great Recession year is interacted with a dummy for the state: that is, state fixed effects interacted
11:315:27300:22:22:71:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with separate dummies for each recessionary year: 2007, 2008, 2009.10This specification allows
11:316:27394:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:state level outcomes to respond arbitrarily to each recession, but as a consequence of the inclusion
11:317:27494:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the state-specific recession-year dummies, the identifying variation in such specifications is largely
11:318:27599:22:41:72:250:160:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:limited to non-recessionary periods.11
11:319:27637:41:11:83:364:119:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:10These correspond to CPS survey years 1991, 1992, 2002, 2008-2010.
11:320:27704:11:15:83:539:108:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:11An added concern raised by Neumark et al. (2014) is that recessionary periods can influence the estimation
11:321:27812:15:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:of state-specific trends. As Allegretto et al. (2017) argue, this too can be handled by the inclusion of state-specific
11:322:27931:11:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:recession-year dummies. In studying minimum wage effects on welfare caseloads, Page et al. (2005) also use state-specific
11:323:28052:10:0:72:440:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:business cycle controls, although they interact the unemployment rate with state dummies.
12:324:28143:0:40:88:307:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The most saturated specification is as follows:
12:325:28190:40:0:86:112:669:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f11:Icit=

12:328:28201:0:40:139:540:669:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:αckln(MWs(i)t−k) +XitΛc+Ws(i)tΨc+μcs(i)+θcd(i)t+ρcr(t)s(i)+σs(i)t+-cit(2)
12:329:28274:40:22:88:539:629:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Besides equations 1 and 2, I also show results from all of the six intermediate specifications with
12:330:28373:22:22:72:540:607:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:combinations of the three sets of controls (division-specific year effects, state-specific recession-year
12:331:28478:22:22:72:541:585:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effects, and state-specific linear trends), and discuss the full range of estimates.12Additionally,
12:332:28577:22:21:71:539:563:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:I assess the relative contribution of each of the three sets of controls in explaining the difference
12:333:28678:21:22:72:276:542:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:between estimates from equations 1 and 2.
12:334:28719:22:22:88:539:520:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:I estimate a series of regressions for alternative income cutoffs. In the main tables, I report the
12:335:28818:22:22:72:540:498:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:impact of minimum wages on the shares below the following cutoffs: 0.5, 0.75, 1, 1.25, 1.5, and 1.75
12:336:28918:22:22:72:540:476:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:times the federal poverty threshold. In the figures, I show the effects for each threshold between 0.5
12:337:29020:22:22:72:540:454:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and 3.5 times the poverty threshold in increments of 0.1. Note that 3.5 times the threshold exceeds
12:338:29119:22:22:72:540:432:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the median income-to-needs ratio in the sample (3.04). Consequently, these estimates characterize
12:339:29216:22:22:72:540:410:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the impact of the policy on the bottom half of the equivalized family income distribution. The
12:340:29310:22:22:72:540:388:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:estimates for cutoffs near the middle of the distribution are also useful as falsification tests, since we
12:341:29416:22:37:72:450:366:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:do not expect the minimum wage to substantially affect incomes in that range.
12:342:29493:37:29:72:276:329:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f14:Unconditional quantile partial effects
12:343:29531:29:22:71:540:300:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:When we estimate the impact of a policy on the proportion of individuals below various income
12:344:29624:22:22:71:539:278:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cutoffs, and do so for a large number of such cutoffs, the semi-elasticities show the effect of a
12:345:29721:22:22:72:540:256:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:log point increase in the minimum wage on the cumulative distribution function (CDF) of family
12:346:29815:22:22:72:542:234:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:incomes. This is an example ofdistribution regressionsas discussed in Chernozhukov et al. (2013).
12:347:29912:22:22:72:540:212:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Moreover, if we have estimates for the impact of the policy on the CDF for all values of an outcome
12:348:30011:22:22:72:539:190:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:y, we can then invert the impact of the policy on the CDF to estimate the effect of the policy on a
12:349:30110:22:21:72:540:168:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:particular quantileQτofy.Figure 1 illustrates the concept:FA(y)is the actual CDF of the outcome
12:350:30205:21:22:72:539:147:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:y, say equivalized family income. The functionFB(y)represents the counterfactual CDF, showing
12:351:30298:22:22:72:540:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the distribution that would occur were there to be a small increase in the minimum wage. Under
12:352:30392:22:28:72:539:103:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the assumption of conditional independence of the treatment,FB(y)is estimable using distribution
12:353:30488:28:0:83:447:75:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:12Using quadratic instead of linear trends in the saturated model produces similar results.
13:354:30581:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:regressions such as equations 1 or 2 of the outcomeIc=1(y)on the treatment, along with a set of
13:355:30676:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:covariates, for every value ofc. The resulting estimates would fully characterize the impact of the
13:356:30775:22:22:72:539:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:treatment on the CDF ofy, i.e.,FB(y)−FA(y), and hence form an estimate of the counterfactual
13:357:30867:22:22:72:163:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:distributionFB(y).
13:358:30885:22:22:88:539:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Say we are interested in the effect of the policy on theτthquantile of the outcomey. The
13:359:30973:22:22:72:542:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:unconditional quantile partial effect (UQPE) estimand is defined as:QB,τ−QA,τ=F−1B(τ)−F−1A(τ).
13:360:31067:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:It is a partial effect of minimum wages, since the distribution regressions used to estimate the
13:361:31163:22:22:72:539:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:counterfactual,FB(y), hold other covariates constant. It is an unconditional quantile effect because
13:362:31263:22:22:72:541:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:it measures the impact of the policy on quantiles of the unconditional (or marginal) distribution ofy,
13:363:31365:22:22:71:539:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:which in the minimum wage context is of greater policy relevance than the conditional quantile partial
13:364:31467:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effect (CQPE) that is the estimand associated with the quantile regression (Koenker and Bassett
13:365:31562:22:22:71:539:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f9:1978). The latter represents the impact of the treatment on theτthquantile of the distribution ofy
13:366:31660:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:conditional on covariates. For example, the CQPE informs us of the impact of minimum wages on
13:367:31753:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:those with low family incomes within their educational group—be they college graduates or without
13:368:31850:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a high school degree. However, when thinking about distributional effects of minimum wages, we
13:369:31944:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:are not as interested in the impact of minimum wages on college graduates with unusually low
13:370:32036:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:family incomes–i.e., who are poor relative to other college graduates. We are more interested in the
13:371:32136:22:22:72:539:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f4:impact on those with low incomes in an absolute (or unconditional) sense.13We do wish tocontrol
13:372:32231:22:22:72:539:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f3:forfactors like education, but do not wish toconditionthe distributional statistic on (e.g., define
13:373:32330:22:22:70:539:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:“low income” based on) those factors. The UQPE,QB,τ−QA,τ, controls for covariates, but does
13:374:32421:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:not define the quantiles based on them; hence, it captures the effect of the policy on the bottom
13:375:32518:22:22:72:254:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quantiles of the marginal distribution.
13:376:32557:22:22:88:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:It is possible to estimate the UQPE for theτthquantile by (1) estimating the effect of the policy
13:377:32654:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:on the proportions under a large set of cutoffs,c, and forming an estimate for the counterfactual
13:378:32751:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:distributionFB(τ), and then (2) globally inverting that distribution function and obtain an estimate
13:379:32851:22:21:72:539:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:forF−1B(τ)and hence an estimate forF−1B(τ)−F−1A(τ). This procedure is feasible, and outlined in
13:380:32946:21:31:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Chernozhukov et al. (2013). However, it is computationally demanding as it requires estimating a
13:381:33042:31:15:83:540:108:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:13To be clear, both the UQPE and CQPE measure the effect of the treatment on low income quantiles, and not
13:382:33148:15:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:specifically on people who would have earned low incomes (in either a conditional or an unconditional sense) absent
13:383:33263:11:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the policy. The two concepts coincide only under the additional assumption of rank invariance, i.e., that the treatment
13:384:33382:10:0:72:237:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:does not alter the ranking of individuals.
14:385:33426:0:22:71:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:very large number of distribution regressions to globally invertFB(y)and estimate the quantile
14:386:33520:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effects. As described in Firpo et al. (2009) and Fortin et al. (2011), we can instead invert the
14:387:33616:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:counterfactual distribution function using a local linear approximation. Figure 1 provides the
14:388:33710:22:22:72:539:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:intuition behind this approach. We begin by defining a cutoffcassociated with quantileτsuch
14:389:33801:22:22:72:539:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:thatFA(c) =τusing the actual distribution. Next, we estimate the effect of the policy on the
14:390:33893:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:proportion belowcusing a single distribution regression. The effect on the proportion is graphically
14:391:33993:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:represented as∆ =(FB(c)−FA(c))in Figure 1. Now, the quantityQB,τ−QA,τcan be locally
14:392:34076:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:approximated by the product of the vertical distance−∆ =−(FB(c)−FA(c))divided by the slope
14:393:34166:22:22:71:542:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the distribution function atFA(c) =τ, which is just the PDF ofyat theτthquantile:fA(F−1A(τ)).
14:394:34262:22:22:71:539:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The green dashed triangle shows the geometry of this local linear approximation, which can be
14:395:34355:22:22:71:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:written asUQPE≈−FB(c)−FA(c)fA(c). While the global inversion would require us to estimate a large
14:396:34452:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:number of regressions for different values ofcin order to obtain the estimate for a single quantile
14:397:34551:22:21:72:424:445:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:Qτ, only one regression is needed for each quantile when inverting locally.
14:398:34626:21:22:88:539:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The key simplification of taking a linear approximation to the counterfactual CDF works well
14:399:34718:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for a relatively continuous treatment with a substantial variation in treatment intensity, and less
14:400:34817:22:22:71:539:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:well for lumpy or discrete treatments. Given the fairly continuous variation in minimum wages, the
14:401:34915:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:approximation error is unlikely to be a major concern here. Later in this section, I discuss a few
14:402:35013:22:22:72:494:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:additional features of the data that further reduce the scope of the approximation error.
14:403:35102:22:22:88:539:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To operationalize the estimation, following Firpo et al. (2009), I use as the dependent variable
