15:425:35861:0:22:88:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:I estimate a series of regressions for alternative quantiles,Qτ. Again, I use a range of controls
15:426:35958:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for time-varying heterogeneity across eight different specifications. The most saturated specification
15:427:36060:22:56:72:132:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is as follows:
15:428:36074:56:15:104:177:609:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f11:RIF(y′it,Qτ) =
15:429:36088:15:10:88:103:594:10:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f13:∑3
15:430:36090:10:0:99:509:584:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f10:k=−1γτ,kln(MWs(i),t−k) +XitΛτ+Ws(i)tΦτ+πτs(i)+θτd(i)t+στs(i)t+ρτr(t)s(i)+-τit
15:431:36167:0:47:526:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(4)
15:432:36170:47:0:88:149:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f11:Here,γLRτ=
15:433:36180:0:10:151:166:559:10:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f13:∑3
15:434:36182:10:0:162:530:549:8:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f9:k=0γτkis the minimum wage long run semi-elasticity for the UQPE at theτ
15:435:36253:0:26:531:539:556:8:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f10:th
15:436:36255:26:22:72:540:530:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quantile of equivalized family income. Note thatγLRτ=FPTf(c(τ))×αLRc(τ), so there is a one-to-one
15:437:36352:22:22:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:correspondence between the estimates from equations 2 and 4. To obtain the minimum wage
15:438:36439:22:0:72:496:486:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f10:elasticity for theτthincome quantile, we divideγLRτbyQτ=c(τ)×FPT, soηLRτ=γ
15:439:36513:0:13:497:499:494:6:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f12:LRτ
15:440:36516:13:0:479:524:481:8:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f3:c(τ)×FPT.
15:441:36525:0:26:529:537:490:8:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:14
15:442:36527:26:22:88:539:464:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A number of features of the data make it attractive for the application of the RIF-UQPE
15:443:36614:22:22:72:540:442:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:approach. Appendix Table B.1 and Figure B.2 show the cumulative distribution function for the
15:444:36707:22:22:72:542:420:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income-to-needs ratio. I note that the CDF is nearly linear in the bottom half of the distribution,
15:445:36806:22:22:72:540:398:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:especially between income-to-needs ratios of 0.75 and 2.50, which roughly correspond to the 10th
15:446:36902:22:22:72:540:376:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and 40th percentiles: in this range the PDF is essentially flat.15The linearity of the actual CDF (in
15:447:37003:22:21:72:540:354:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:combination with a continuous treatment) reduces the scope of the error from a linear approximation
15:448:37102:21:22:71:379:333:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:when inverting the counterfactual CDF using the RIF approach.
15:449:37163:22:22:88:539:311:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Additionally, Appendix Figure B.3 shows that the income quantiles at the bottom of the
15:450:37249:22:22:71:539:289:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:distribution have been fairly stationary over the past three decades, although they do exhibit
15:451:37343:22:22:72:540:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cyclical tendencies. Appendix Figure B.3 also shows that the probability densities at the associated
15:452:37443:22:22:72:540:245:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income-to-needs cutoffs (fA(c(τ))have also been fairly stable over time, with the possible exception
15:453:37543:22:22:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the 5th quantile. The relative stability of the income-to-needs quantiles and densities is relevant
15:454:37645:22:22:72:541:201:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for interpreting the UQPE estimates. The estimation of the UQPE for a particular quantile,τ,
15:455:37737:22:22:72:540:179:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is based on changes in the proportion below the income-to-needs cutoffc(τ)associated with that
15:456:37831:22:27:72:542:157:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quantile, along with the probability density of the income-to-needs ratio at that cutoff,fA(c(τ)).
15:457:37929:27:15:83:540:130:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:14I find that the estimation error inf(Qτ)contributes trivially to the overall variance of theηLRτ. Using the delta
15:458:38044:15:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:method, accounting for the estimation of the density around the cutoff increases the standard error ofηLRτtypically by
15:459:38162:11:11:71:539:104:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:less than 0.1%. For this reason, the results in this paper do not explicitly adjust the standard errors for the estimation
15:460:38284:11:7:72:110:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:off(Qτ).
15:461:38292:7:14:83:539:86:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:15The kernel density estimation uses an Epanechnikov kernel and the STATA default bandwidth based on Silverman’s
15:462:38404:14:0:72:130:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:rule-of-thumb.
16:463:38420:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Bothc(τ)andfA(y)are calculated by averaging over the entire sample. The relative stability of the
16:464:38517:22:22:72:539:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:mapping betweencandτover this period suggests that the estimated impact on income around a
16:465:38607:22:22:72:432:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:given cutoffcis referring to roughly the same quantile over this full period.
16:466:38684:22:22:88:541:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f11:Finally, the use of the full-sample distribution to estimate the cutoffc(τ)and the densityfA(c)
16:467:38779:22:22:72:542:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:may be an issue if the treatment and control units had very different income distributions. However,
16:468:38879:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:all states receive treatment at some point during the sample, and the variation in minimum wages
16:469:38975:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is fairly continuous and widespread; therefore, the the sample-averaged cutoffs and densities are
16:470:39072:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:broadly representative of where the minimum wage variation is coming from. Overall, the nature
16:471:39166:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of both the treatment as well as the outcome facilitate the application of the RIF approach to a
16:472:39262:22:38:72:224:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:repeated cross-sectional setting.
16:473:39295:38:29:72:225:473:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:2.3  Descriptive statistics
16:474:39322:29:21:71:540:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Table 1 shows shares of the non-elderly population, as well as eight key demographic groups under
16:475:39419:21:22:72:542:423:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:alternative income cutoffs, which range between 0.5 and 1.75 times the federal poverty threshold.
16:476:39516:22:22:71:539:401:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To clarify, row 3 shows the poverty rates, while row 5 shows the share with income below 1.5 times
16:477:39614:22:22:72:178:379:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the poverty threshold.
16:478:39636:22:22:88:539:357:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:For non-elderly adults as a whole, the poverty rate averaged at 0.136 during the 1984-2013
16:479:39726:22:22:71:539:335:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:period. Including elderly in the sample decreases it slightly to 0.132. Individuals without a high
16:480:39824:22:22:72:540:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:school degree (0.214) as well as those with high school or lesser schooling (0.179) had greater rates of
16:481:39928:22:22:72:540:291:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:poverty. The poverty rate for single mothers (0.224), black/Latino individuals (0.263), and children
16:482:40028:22:22:70:539:269:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(0.195) were all higher than the average. Poverty rate among adults (0.112), on the other hand, is
16:483:40126:22:22:72:540:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:smaller than other groups. These patterns are as expected, and are qualitatively similar when we
16:484:40222:22:45:72:299:225:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:consider 50% or 150% of the poverty threshold.
16:485:40268:45:34:72:224:180:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:3  Empirical findings
16:486:40289:34:29:72:458:146:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:3.1  Main results for shares below multiples of poverty threshold
16:487:40354:29:22:71:539:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Table 2 provides the estimates for the impact of minimum wages on the shares below various multiples
16:488:40454:22:21:72:540:95:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the federal poverty threshold. For ease of interpretation, I report the estimates as elasticities
16:489:40554:21:0:72:539:74:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f3:βMRcandβLRcby dividing the sum of regression coefficients by the sample proportion under each
17:490:40649:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cutoff; this is true both for the point estimate and the standard errors. I show estimates using the
17:491:40749:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:specification which includes (a) division-specific year effects, (b) state-specific Great Recession-year
17:492:40853:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:dummies, and (c) state-specific linear trends. In Section 3.4, I show that the general findings of
17:493:40951:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:poverty reduction are robust to virtually all forms of controls for time-varying heterogeneity used in
17:494:41053:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:this literature, including the simple two-way fixed effects model. However, as I also show in Section
17:495:41154:22:22:71:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:3.4, the saturated model performs the best in terms of falsification tests, which is why I use it as my
17:496:41257:22:22:72:180:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:preferred specification.
17:497:41281:22:22:88:539:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Overall, there is strong evidence that minimum wage increases reduce the share of individuals
17:498:41374:22:22:71:539:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with low family incomes. The medium-run poverty elasticity is -0.399 (SE=0.126), while the long-run
17:499:41473:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:estimate is -0.446 (SE=0.137), both being statistically significant at the 1 percent level. More
17:500:41569:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:generally, there is a reduction in the shares of individuals with incomes below family income cutoffs
17:501:41670:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:between 50 and 125 percent of the official poverty threshold: the long-run elasticities range between
17:502:41771:22:21:70:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:-0.294 and -0.461, and these are all statistically significant at the 5 percent level (except for the 50
17:503:41875:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:percent cutoff, which is significant at the 10 percent level). Figure 2 provides visual evidence on
17:504:41974:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:how minimum wages affect the bottom half of the family income distribution. The figure reports
17:505:42068:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:elasticities for each multiple of the poverty threshold between 0.5 and 3.5 in increments of 0.1—a
17:506:42166:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:total of 31 regressions. The top panel shows that by the second year after the policy change, there
17:507:42265:22:22:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:are large, statistically significant reductions in the share below cutoffs between 0.5 and 1.2 times
17:508:42365:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the poverty threshold with minimum wage elasticities exceeding -0.5 in magnitude. The elasticities
17:509:42463:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for cutoffs exceeding 1.2 are mostly close to zero, and never statistically significant. The bottom
17:510:42562:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:panel of the figure shows that that long run (3+ year) minimum wage elasticities are sizable and
17:511:42658:22:22:72:542:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:statistically significant for cutoffs between roughly 0.6 and 1.4 times the poverty threshold. However,
17:512:42761:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:there is some additional reduction in the shares below cutoffs between 1.4 and 2 times the poverty
17:513:42859:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:threshold. The elasticities subsequently decline in magnitude, and are close to zero for cutoffs of
17:514:42958:22:22:71:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:2.75 times the poverty threshold or greater. Overall, there is an indication that the medium run (2
17:515:43057:22:21:71:539:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:year) effects are more concentrated at lower incomes than longer run effects. The lagged effects
17:516:43153:21:22:71:539:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:higher up in the family income distribution could be consistent with a lagged spillover effect of
17:517:43250:22:22:72:272:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:minimum wages on the wage distribution.
17:518:43289:22:22:88:539:95:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:While the baseline specifications use 1 year of lead and 3 years of lags, to further assess the issue
17:519:43390:22:0:72:540:73:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of parallel trends, I also estimate a longer distributed lag model with 3 leads and 3 lags. Figure 3
18:520:43492:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:reports the cumulative response elasticities by successively adding the leads and lags, normalizing
18:521:43591:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the elasticity to be zero at event time equal to -1. The top panel shows the changes for the share
18:522:43689:22:22:72:542:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:below the federal poverty threshold: the share is stable in the 3 years prior to the policy change,
18:523:43788:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:but starts falling starting the year of the minimum wage increase, and reaches its maximum impact
18:524:43885:22:22:71:539:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:2 years after the change. In contrast, the share below 3 times the federal poverty threshold shows
18:525:43983:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:no systematic movement: the cumulative response is close to zero for the three years prior to the
18:526:44080:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:policy change, and straddles zero subsequently. Overall, this evidence on timing provides additional
18:527:44180:22:22:71:232:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:validation for the research design.
18:528:44215:22:22:88:539:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To assess possible heterogeneity in the effect of the policy, Table 3 shows minimum wage
18:529:44303:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:elasticities for the shares below alternative family income cutoffs for various demographic groups
18:530:44401:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:defined using education, age, gender, race, presence of kids, and marital status. For all groups, I
18:531:44500:22:22:72:542:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:find sizable reductions in the proportions under 50, 75, 100 and 125 percent of the poverty threshold.
18:532:44602:22:21:71:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The long run estimates of these 32 elasticities (8 groups with 4 cutoffs each) range between -0.225
18:533:44701:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and -0.872, and 28 are statistically significant at least at the 10 percent level. As compared to our
18:534:44802:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:previous estimates for non-elderly individuals (-0.446), the poverty rate elasticities are quite similar
18:535:44906:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for children (-0.499), those without a high school degree (-0.481), those with high school or lesser
18:536:45006:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:schooling (-0.474), all individuals including elderly (-0.436), all adults (-0.375), and individuals
18:537:45106:22:22:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:under thirty without a high school degree (-0.432). In contrast, they are are somewhat smaller
18:538:45200:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in magnitude for single mothers (-0.327), and substantially larger in magnitude for black and
18:539:45293:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Latino individuals (-0.872). The reductions in low-income shares extend somewhat further up the
18:540:45388:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:distribution for black and Latino individuals, children under 18, and those under 30 without a high
18:541:45487:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:school degree; for these groups, there are substantial and statistically significant reductions for up
18:542:45589:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to 175 percent of the poverty threshold. The key conclusion from these findings is that when we
18:543:45684:22:22:72:542:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:focus on disadvantaged groups such as black or Latino individuals, or those with lesser education,
18:544:45782:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the anti-poverty impact of minimum wages appears to be similar or somewhat greater; however, for
18:545:45878:22:21:72:449:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:another disadvantaged group (single mothers) the impact is somewhat smaller.
18:546:45954:21:22:88:539:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Next, I compare my findings with what the existing research suggests about heterogeneous
18:547:46042:22:22:72:542:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:impact by age, single mother status, education, and race, as summarized in Appendix Table A.1.
18:548:46136:22:22:72:542:95:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:First, if we take the poverty rate elasticities for groups under 20 years of age in the literature,
18:549:46235:22:0:72:542:73:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Morgan and Kickham (2001) and Addison and Blackburn (1999) also find a substantial effect of,
19:550:46330:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:respectively, -0.39 and -0.39 (averaged across specifcations for teens). While my estimate for all
19:551:46428:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:children are somewhat larger in magnitude (-0.499), both existing work and results in this paper
19:552:46524:22:22:72:490:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:point toward a substantial poverty reducing impact of minimum wages among children.
19:553:46607:22:22:88:541:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Second, for single mothers, I find elasticities for the proportion under the poverty line of -0.327,
19:554:46707:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and under one-half poverty line of -0.458, which as noted above are somewhat smaller than the
19:555:46800:22:22:72:542:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:population overall; they are also imprecise and not statistically significant at conventional levels.
19:556:46901:22:22:71:539:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The implied elasticities in Neumark (2016) for 21-44 year old single women with kids range between
19:557:46999:22:22:70:541:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:-0.14 and -0.30 depending on specification. These estimates are broadly similar to what I find,
19:558:47094:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:though I note the imprecision in both sets of estimates. Sabia (2008) finds a range of elasticities
19:559:47193:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:between -0.28 and -0.17 for single mothers, depending on the mother’s education level. Burkhauser
19:560:47290:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and Sabia (2007) find poverty rate elasticities for single mothers between -0.21 and -0.07 depending
19:561:47390:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:on specification. DeFina (2008) finds poverty rate elasticities in woman headed households with kids
19:562:47490:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of -0.42 (-0.35 when restricting to mothers without a college education). Finally, Gundersen and
19:563:47586:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Ziliak (2004) finds very small effects for woman headed households (-0.02). If we take an average of
19:564:47686:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the poverty rate elasticities for single mothers (or woman heads of households) across these five
19:565:47783:22:22:72:465:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:studies, we get an average elasticity of -0.18, as compared to my estimate of -0.30.
19:566:47867:22:22:88:539:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The third comparison concerns heterogeneity in the effect by levels of education. I find poverty
19:567:47963:22:22:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:elasticities for those without a high school degree (-0.481), or with high school or lesser schooling
19:568:48064:22:22:70:539:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(-0.474) that are comparable to the overall estimate (-0.446). Neumark (2016) provides estimates
19:569:48160:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for those 21 years or age or older by education: the unrestricted estimates range between -0.11 and
19:570:48259:22:22:70:539:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:-0.15, while for those with high school or lesser education, they range between -0.01 and -0.19; none
19:571:48360:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of these are statistically significant. Sabia (2008) finds somewhat larger reductions in the poverty
19:572:48460:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rate for single mothers without a high school degree (-0.28) than those with (-0.17), although neither
19:573:48562:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:estimate is statistically significant. In contrast, restricting to those with less education tends to
19:574:48663:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:slightly diminish the effects in DeFina (2008), though they continue to be sizable (changing from
19:575:48760:22:21:70:539:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:-0.42 to -0.35). The estimates in Sabia and Nielsen (2015) are highly imprecise and the impact of
19:576:48857:21:22:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:conditioning on education levels is contradictory across specifications. Finally, while Addison and
19:577:48956:22:22:72:540:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Blackburn (1999) do not provide comparable estimates by levels of education, averages across their
19:578:49054:22:22:72:540:95:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:specifications do suggest a somewhat large elasticity (-0.45) for individuals who did not complete
19:579:49152:22:0:72:540:73:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:junior high school. While the estimates in the literature do not paint to a clear picture, on balance
20:580:49255:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:they do not suggest that the poverty reducing effect of minimum wages is smaller among those with
20:581:49352:22:22:72:340:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:less education. That is consistent with what I find here.
20:582:49409:22:22:88:539:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The fourth, and final, comparison concerns heterogeneity by race. Here, I find clear evidence of
20:583:49505:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:substantially stronger reduction in poverty, and near poverty, among black or Latino individuals as
20:584:49604:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:compared to the population as a whole. Gundersen and Ziliak (2004) also find a slightly larger effect
20:585:49705:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the black population—though the magnitude is still very small (-0.06). Finally, the estimates in
20:586:49804:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Sabia and Nielsen (2015) are, again, imprecise and qualitatively differ by specification. This paper
20:587:49904:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:provides sharper evidence than available in existing work that minimum wages tend to raise bottom
20:588:50001:22:38:72:352:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:incomes more strongly for African Americans and Latinos.
20:589:50057:38:29:72:299:495:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:3.2  Effect on family income quantiles
20:590:50095:29:22:71:540:466:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We can use the impact of minimum wages on the cumulative distribution of family income to
20:591:50184:22:21:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:estimate the impact on family income quantiles. Figure 4 shows the sample average CDF of family
20:592:50279:21:22:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income, along with the counterfactual distribution. In the top scale of the figure, income is shown
20:593:50378:22:22:72:540:401:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:as multiples of the federal poverty threshold,y. The bottom scale shows income in dollar amounts
20:594:50474:22:22:72:542:379:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:obtained by multiplyingyby the sample average of the real federal poverty threshold ($22,476).
20:595:50568:22:22:72:540:357:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Here the counterfactual distribution at incomecis calculated asF(c) +αLRc,whereF(c)is the CDF
20:596:50661:22:22:72:539:335:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:averaged over the entire sample, andαLRcis the 3+ year minimum wage semi-elasticity estimated
20:597:50754:22:22:72:540:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:from equation (2). In other words, it is the counterfactual CDF with a log point increase in the
20:598:50850:22:22:72:539:291:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:minimum wage. The figure is based on 31 separate regressions estimated for cutoffscbetween
20:599:50940:22:22:72:540:269:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:0.5 and 3.5 in increments of 0.1 using the preferred specification. This is just a different way of
20:600:51039:22:22:72:540:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:reporting the estimates shown in Figure 2, which instead showed the impact as elasticities. In
20:601:51133:22:22:72:540:225:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:both figures, we can see that there is a statistically significant and quantitatively substantial shift
20:602:51236:22:22:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the CDF for incomes between 0.5 and 1.75 times the poverty threshold. Overall, an increase
20:603:51329:22:22:72:540:181:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the minimum wage seems to improve the family income distribution in the sense of first order
20:604:51424:22:21:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:stochastic dominance. By juxtaposing the actual and counterfactual CDF, we can also visually
20:605:51516:21:22:72:540:138:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:assess the impact by quantiles (the vertical axis). By considering the horizontal distance between the
20:606:51618:22:22:72:540:116:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:actual and counterfactual CDFs, we can infer that there is clear, statistically significant, increases
20:607:51720:22:22:72:540:94:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in incomes between the 10th and 20th percentiles. And that above the 40th percentile, the changes
20:608:51817:22:0:70:288:72:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(horizontal distance) are mostly close to zero.
21:609:51866:0:22:88:541:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This exercise illustrates the key idea behind estimating the unconditional quantile partial effects.
21:610:51966:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In principle, we can estimate the quantiles by globally inverting the CDF as we did visually when
21:611:52063:22:22:72:542:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:inspecting Figure 4. This is similar to the approach in Chernozhukov et al. (2013). While feasible,
21:612:52162:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:this requires estimating a large number of regressions, even when estimating the effect for a single
21:613:52262:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quantile. Therefore, the global inversion can be computationally demanding, especially as we wish
21:614:52359:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:to estimate it for many specifications with a large set of fixed effects and for different income
21:615:52456:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:definitions, and using individual level data. For this reason, I use the RIF approach proposed by
21:616:52553:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Firpo et al. (2009). We approximate the horizontal distance between the actual and counterfactual
21:617:52650:22:22:72:542:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:CDFs at quantileqby dividing the vertical distance between the two by the PDF atq=F−1(c).
21:618:52739:22:22:71:539:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This requires us to estimate only a single regression per quantile. The unconditional quantile
21:619:52833:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:partial effects (βτ)are estimated using equation 3, or analogous regressions for the less saturated
21:620:52932:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:specifications. To convert the UQPEs into elasticities (ητ), they are subsequently divided by the
21:621:53029:22:21:72:349:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income-to-needs cutoffs corresponding to a given quantile.
21:622:53087:21:22:88:539:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Figure 5 shows the long-run minimum wage elasticities for each family income quantile between
21:623:53180:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:5 and 50 using the preferred specification. We find substantial and statistically significant effects
21:624:53281:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for quantiles between the 7th and 20th, declining sharply by the 35th quantile. The elasticities
21:625:53377:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:around the median of the family income distribution straddle zero. The figure provides compelling
21:626:53474:22:22:71:541:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:visual evidence that minimum wage policies tend to raise income at the bottom of the distribution,
21:627:53572:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:consistent with evidence on the CDF in Figure 4. Column 2 of Table 4 reports the magnitudes
21:628:53663:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the medium and long-run elasticities for the baseline (cash) income definition. The long run
21:629:53758:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:elasticities are 0.273, 0.359, 0.332, 0.152, and 0.164 for the 5th, 10th, 15th, 20th and 25th quantiles
21:630:53861:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of equivalized family incomes, respectively. The 10th, 15th, and 25th quantiles are statistically
21:631:53958:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:significant at least at the 5 percent level, while the 20th quantile is significant at the 10 percent
21:632:54059:22:18:72:104:204:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:level.16
21:633:54067:18:23:88:96:186:8:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:17
21:634:54069:23:15:83:541:163:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:16As noted above, globally inverting the CDF is computationally intensive, and especially for conducting inference.
21:635:54184:15:11:72:540:148:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:However, the estimates are broadly similar. For example, the elasticities for 10th, 15th, 20th, 30th, 40th, and 50th
21:636:54300:11:11:72:541:137:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:quantiles when inverting globally are 0.44, 0.26, 0.18, 0.09, 0.05, 0.08, while the locally inverted estimates are 0.36,
21:637:54420:11:7:72:365:126:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:0.33, 0.15, 0.09, 0.05, 0.02, respectively. (Results not reported in tables.)
21:638:54497:7:15:83:539:119:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:17These are based on point-wise confidence intervals. Additionally, I implement the bootstrap-based approach of
21:639:54608:15:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:Lehrer et al. (2016)—which identifies the ranges of the outcome distribution that exhibit positive treatment effects
21:640:54724:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:accounting for possible multiple testing concerns. The more conservative inference of Lehrer et al. control for the
21:641:54839:11:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:family-wise error rate, which here is the probability that we mistakenly declare a positive UQPE for at least one
21:642:54952:10:0:72:540:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:quantile in the considered range. When I consider the quantiles 10, 15, 20, 25, and 30, I find that the 10th and 15th
22:643:55071:0:22:88:541:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:So far, our income defintion has corresponded to that used in the official poverty definition,
22:644:55165:22:22:71:539:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:which limits to cash-based incomes. Next, we expand the income definition, and estimate minimum
22:645:55260:22:22:71:539:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wage elasticities for quantiles of family income inclusive of tax credits and non-cash transfers. These
22:646:55363:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:elasticities are reported in column 4 of Table 4, and are generally smaller than those using pre-tax
22:647:55463:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cash income (column 2). Specifically, averaged across the 10th and the 15th quantiles—where
22:648:55554:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:there is a sizable effect—the elasticities are 69% and 60% as large from using the expanded income
22:649:55652:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:definition for the medium and long run, respectively. Figure 6 shows the elasticities visually for
22:650:55750:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:each quantile between 5 and 50 using the preferred specification, where we continue to find sizable
22:651:55849:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and statistically significant effects between 7th and 20th quantiles. However, the elasticities using
22:652:55950:22:22:72:460:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:expanded income are about 60% as large as those in Figure 5 for those quantiles.
22:653:56030:22:22:88:539:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:While the elasticities are useful in understanding how responsive income is to minimum wages
22:654:56122:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for various quantiles, they are less useful for assessing how much of the cash income gain is being
22:655:56221:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:offset by a loss in tax credits or non-cash transfers. This is because the proportionate change in
22:656:56319:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:cash versus expanded incomes is also driven by the fact that the expanded incomes are larger: so a
22:657:56417:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:$1 increase in income due to minimum wages is a smaller share of expanded income, just because
22:658:56511:22:22:72:542:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the $1 is divided by a larger denominator. For example, the 15th quantile in cash income is $24,123;
22:659:56611:22:22:71:542:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:when we expand the income definition to include non-cash transfers and tax credits, it is $27,423.
22:660:56709:22:22:71:539:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Therefore, even if the income gains using the two definition are identical, the elasticity using the
22:661:56809:22:22:72:351:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:expanded income definition would be around 12% smaller.
22:662:56864:22:22:88:539:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To better capture the extent of offset, Table 4 reports the minimum wage effect on the level
22:663:56956:22:22:72:542:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of real incomes (i.e., the semi-elasticities,γτ) for progressively more expansive income definitions.
22:664:57057:22:22:71:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:When we consider all 5 quantiles (5th, 10th, 15th, 20th, 25th and 30th), the increase in expanded
22:665:57154:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income including tax credits and non-cash transfers is around 66% as large. About a third of the loss
22:666:57255:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:is due to reduced non-cash transfers (column 3) while the remaining two thirds is due to reduction in
22:667:57356:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tax credits (column 5). However, there is an interesting difference in where in the income distribution
22:668:57459:22:21:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:these two losses occur. To see this more easily, I plot the semi-elasticities from the three income
22:669:57558:21:22:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:definitions in Figure 7. The loss due to reduced non-cash transfers is highly concentrated between
22:670:57656:22:24:72:540:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the 14th and 16th quantiles, around or just above the federal poverty threshold. This is consistent
22:671:57755:24:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:quantile effect are statistically significant at the 5 percent level. This contrasts with the point-wise CI which are
22:672:57872:11:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:significant for the 10th, 15th and 25th quantiles. Overall, the conclusion that there are positive effects at the 10th and
22:673:57994:10:0:71:359:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:15th quantiles do not appear to be driven by multiple-testing concerns.
23:674:58067:0:22:71:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with the nature of eligibility requirements of non-cash assistance programs: for instance, typically
23:675:58167:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:only individuals with income at or lower than 130% of the federal poverty threshold are eligible for
23:676:58267:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:SNAP. As a result, some individuals with incomes just below the eligibility threshold can lose the
23:677:58365:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:benefits due to higher earnings. Figure 7 provides compelling evidence on the importance of these
23:678:58462:22:22:72:542:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:offsets: at the 15th quantile, there is a 40% offset to the income gain due to loss in public assistance,
23:679:58567:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:mostly due to reduced non-cash transfers. In contrast, at 10th or 20th quantiles, the offset in income
23:680:58669:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:gains due to loss in public assistance was only around 15%. Moreover, while the loss in non-cash
23:681:58765:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:transfers is relatively more concentrated around the 15th quantile, the loss due to tax credits is
23:682:58863:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:more uniform across the income distribution. This likely reflects the fact that the EITC phase-out
23:683:58961:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:range is more spread out. The findings on offsets is also consistent with simulation results from
23:684:59058:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Maag and Carasso (2013) who tend to find that the effective marginal tax rate (after accounting for
23:685:59157:22:22:72:539:467:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:transfers) on earnings is often quite high between 100 and 150% of the federal poverty threshold.18
23:686:59256:22:21:88:539:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Finally, Table 4 also shows that the offsets in public assistance appear to be larger in the long
23:687:59353:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:run. This could potentially reflect a behavioral response in utilization: for example, higher incomes
23:688:59454:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:could reduce SNAP take-up rate and not the eligibility rate, and changes in take-up behavior can
23:689:59550:22:22:72:420:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:take longer to adjust than the mechanical effects of changes in eligibility.
23:690:59626:22:22:88:539:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:While use of the thirty years of data provides us with greater precision, one may wonder whether
23:691:59722:22:22:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the patterns are similar in more recent times. In particular, when it comes to tax credits and
23:692:59816:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:transfers, EITC expansion of 1992 and welfare reform in 1996 are important, and may interact
23:693:59908:22:22:71:539:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with the minimum wage policy. Moreover, there is evidence that target efficiency of minimum
23:694:59999:22:22:71:539:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages has improved over time (Lundstrom, 2016). For these reasons, in Table 5, I show the income
23:695:60095:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:elasticities by quantiles for cash income and expanded income including tax-credits and transfers
23:696:60192:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for subsamples beginning in 1990 as well as 1996. The estimates are quite similar to those from
23:697:60287:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the full sample. For the sample beginning in 1996, the long run elasticities for the 10th and 15th
23:698:60385:22:30:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quantiles when considering cash incomes are 0.447 and 0.503, respectively, and both are statistically
23:699:60486:30:15:83:540:152:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:18That the income gains at the 15th quantile is 40% smaller when using an expanded income definition does not
23:700:60595:15:11:72:540:137:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:necessarily imply that an individual at the 15th quantile of the cash incomes experiences a 40% offset due to lost
23:701:60709:11:11:72:541:126:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:public assistance. Individuals at these quantiles need not be the same (a) before versus after the policy change (b)
23:702:60825:11:11:71:539:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:when considering different types of incomes. We would need to make a rank-invariance assumption to assure that our
23:703:60939:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:findings about quantiles can be interpreted as reflecting impacts on individuals. As an empirical matter, ranks in the
23:704:61057:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:conventional cash income and the expanded incomes are highly correlated. For those in the bottom half of the cash
23:705:61170:11:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:income distribution, the correlation coefficient between the two ranks is 0.99. However, this does not tell us whether
23:706:61288:10:0:72:335:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the policy affects the rank of individuals in the two distributions.
24:707:61358:0:22:72:542:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:significant at the 5% level. For comparison, these elasticities for the full sample are 0.359 and 0.332,
24:708:61462:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:respectively (Table B.4). When using the expanded income definition, the elasticities for these two
24:709:61561:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:quantiles are 0.352 and 0.275 in the 1996-2013 sample, as compared to 0.256 and 0.160 in the full
24:710:61658:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:sample. Estimates from the sample beginning in 1990 are similar. As expected, the estimates for
24:711:61753:22:38:72:471:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the smaller samples are generally less precise, but the magnitudes are quite similar.
24:712:61838:38:29:72:522:583:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:3.3  Robustness to alternative assumptions about unobserved heterogeneity
24:713:61911:29:22:71:539:554:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:To assess how controls for unobserved heterogeneity influence the findings, Figure 8 plots the long
24:714:62010:22:22:72:542:532:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:term minimum wage elasticities for shares below various multiples of the federal poverty threshold.
24:715:62109:22:22:70:540:510:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(The full set of medium and long run coefficients and standard errors are reported in Online Appendix
24:716:62210:22:22:71:539:488:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Table B.3.) I use eight different regression specifications that range from the classic two-way fixed
24:717:62311:22:22:72:541:466:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effects model (panel A, column 1 in Figure 8) to the most saturated specification (panel B, column 4)
24:718:62412:22:21:71:539:444:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:which includes (a) division-specific year effects, (b) state-specific Great Recession-year dummies, and
24:719:62515:21:22:70:539:423:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(c) state-specific linear trends. The six other specifications exhaust all intermediate combinations of
24:720:62618:22:22:72:540:401:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:controls and provide us with evidence on how the inclusion of various types of time-varying controls
24:721:62718:22:22:72:172:379:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:affects the estimates.
24:722:62740:22:22:88:539:357:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Overall, there is robust evidence that minimum wage increases reduce the share of individuals
24:723:62833:22:22:71:540:335:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with low family incomes. For family income cutoffs between 0.50 and 1.25 (i.e., between 50 and 125
24:724:62931:22:22:72:540:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:percent of the official poverty threshold), and across the eight specifications, all 32 of the long run
24:725:63034:22:22:72:540:291:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:estimates (sum of the contemporaneous plus one, two and three year lags in minimum wage) are
24:726:63126:22:22:72:540:269:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:negative in sign, and 29 are statistically significant at least at the 10 percent level. This includes
24:727:63228:22:22:72:540:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:all of the poverty rate elasticities, which are statistically significant at the 5 percent level. While
24:728:63331:22:22:72:540:225:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:all of the estimates are sizable, the more saturated specifications tend to produce estimates with
24:729:63429:22:22:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:somewhat larger magnitudes. For example, the long run poverty elasticity estimate of -0.220 from
24:730:63525:22:22:72:540:181:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the two-way fixed effects estimate (panel A, column 1 of Figure 8) is the smallest in magnitude
24:731:63620:22:21:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:among all eight specifications. In contrast, the estimate with state-trends and division-period FE
24:732:63718:21:22:70:539:138:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:(panel B, column 3) is the largest in magnitude (-0.459); the preferred specification used in the
24:733:63815:22:22:72:353:116:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:paper (panel B, column 4) produces an elasticity of -0.446.
24:734:63874:22:22:88:539:94:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Figure 9 presents analogous evidence on equivalized family income elasticities for quantiles, and
24:735:63971:22:0:72:540:72:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:shows robust evidence across all 8 specifications that minimum wages lead to at least moderate
25:736:64067:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:increases in incomes for the bottom 20 percent of the equivalized family income distribution. (Online
25:737:64168:22:22:71:541:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Appendix Table B.4 reports the full set of estimates and standard errors.) Of the 32 estimates,
25:738:64263:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:all are positive in sign, and 24 are statistically significant at least at the 10 percent level. The 16
25:739:64366:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:estimates for the 10th and the 15th quantiles range between 0.152 and 0.430, and all are statistically
25:740:64468:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:significant at least at the 10 percent level. As before, the two-way fixed effects specification (panel
25:741:64571:22:22:71:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A, column 1) provides the smallest estimated magnitudes, and the inclusion of division-specific year
25:742:64671:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effects and state-specific Great-Recession controls tend to increase the size of the estimates. These
25:743:64772:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:patterns are as expected, since the elasticities for the family income quantiles are simply rescaled
25:744:64872:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:semi-elasticities for the proportions below alternative income-to-needs cutoffs, and the rescaling
25:745:64970:22:22:72:280:511:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:factors are common across specifications.19
25:746:65013:22:22:88:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The range of estimates raises the issue of model selection. There is ana prioricase for using
25:747:65106:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:richer controls that better account for time-varying heterogeneity across states. Allowing for regional
25:748:65209:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:shocks and state-specific trends receives strong support in existing work. For example, Allegretto
25:749:65307:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:et al. (2017) show that the inclusion of these controls mitigates contamination from pre-existing
25:750:65404:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:trends when it comes to estimating the effect of minimum wages on teen employment. They also
25:751:65496:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:provide evidence that synthetic control methods tend to put substantially more weight on nearby
25:752:65591:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:states in constructing a control group, providing additional validity to the intuition that nearby
25:753:65689:22:22:72:542:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:states are better controls. One argument against using more saturated models is the loss of precision:
25:754:65791:22:22:72:539:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that they may lack the statistical power to detect an effect.20However, while the standard errors
25:755:65888:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for the most saturated specifications 8 are larger, the 95% confidence intervals for that specification
25:756:65991:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:does not contain the point estimates using specification 1 for 75 and 100 percent of the federal
25:757:66087:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:poverty threshold. In other words, there is strong indication that the differences in estimates across
25:758:66189:22:22:72:527:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the two specifications are not driven primarily by the imprecision of the more saturated model.
25:759:66284:22:22:88:539:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Beyond this, I consider two types of falsification exercises for model selection. First, I use
25:760:66378:22:30:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the leading values as a falsification test, analogous to tests used in Dube et al. (2010), Allegretto
25:761:66479:30:15:83:539:152:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:19Online Appendix Table B.5 additionally presents family income elasticities using the broader income definition
25:762:66591:15:11:72:540:137:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:including tax credits and non-cash transfers. Averaging across all specifications, the long run estimates for these
25:763:66706:11:11:72:540:126:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:quantiles using the expanded definition are about 60% as large as when using pre-tax cash income, which is similar to
25:764:66823:11:7:72:314:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the 66% estimate I find in the preferred specification above.
25:765:66884:7:15:83:539:108:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:20A second rationale for excluding covariates is that some of them are “bad controls” in the sense of blocking a
25:766:66996:15:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:causal pathway between the treatment and the outcome. As I discussed above, the state-specific linear trends may
25:767:67108:11:10:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:constitute a problem if there are delayed effects of the policy, but I address this issue by including three annual lags in
25:768:67231:10:0:72:135:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:minimum wage.
26:769:67246:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:et al. (2011) and Allegretto et al. (2013). To be clear, the medium and long run estimates do not
26:770:67343:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:include the leading coefficient, so they net out any level differences in the outcome just prior to the
26:771:67446:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:minimum wage increase. However, since a non-zero leading coefficient provides an indication of the
26:772:67544:22:22:71:541:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:violation of parallel trends, such a test can help us assess the validity of particular specifications.
26:773:67647:22:22:71:539:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The results are shown in Table 6. They indicate that specifications 1, 2, 5, 6 all produce positive
26:774:67746:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:leads for the proportion below one-half the poverty line, and these are statistically significant at
26:775:67846:22:22:72:542:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the 5 percent level. Specification 1 also produces positive leads for 1.75 times poverty threshold.
26:776:67945:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In contrast, specifications 3, 4 and 7 tend to produce negative leads for 0.75 times the poverty
26:777:68041:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:threshold. Considering the full range of cutoffs, the most saturated specification 8 usually performs
26:778:68142:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the best when it comes to the leading values falsification test: it is the only specification where
26:779:68241:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:none of the leading coefficients are statistically significant; moreover, this is mostly driven by the
26:780:68343:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:small size of the coefficients and not from a greater imprecision. For example, the absolute value of
26:781:68444:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the mean of all leads in specification 8 is 0.081, while the other specifications range between 0.083
26:782:68545:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and 0.194. Overall, this suggests the most saturated specification may be able to guard against
26:783:68640:22:22:72:487:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:pre-existing trends throughout the income distribution better than less saturated ones.
26:784:68727:22:22:88:539:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In addition, we should not expect minimum wages to affect the proportion earning under 3, 3.5
26:785:68820:22:22:71:539:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:or 4 times the poverty threshold, which roughly corresponds to the 50th, 57th and 64th percentiles
26:786:68918:22:22:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the family income distribution in the national sample. Therefore, reliable specifications should
26:787:69017:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:produce estimates for these cutoffs that are small or close to zero. The bottom panel B of Table 6
26:788:69115:22:22:72:542:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:reports the long run elasticities for shares below these middle and upper income cutoffs. In general,
26:789:69216:22:22:72:542:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:none of the specifications produce statistically significant long run effects, which is reassuring.
26:790:69315:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:However, the most saturated specification produces the smallest magnitudes: the absolute value of
26:791:69412:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the mean for all cutoffs is 0.012 for specification 8, as compared to a range between 0.010 and 0.070
26:792:69513:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:for the other specifications. Overall, the most saturated specification 8 performs very well on the
26:793:69612:22:22:72:464:182:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f5:falsification exercises, while the results from the intermediate specifications vary.21
26:794:69699:22:30:88:539:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Therefore, based both ona priorigrounds as including the richest set of controls for time-varying
26:795:69796:30:15:83:540:130:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:21Additional results (not reported in the tables) also suggests that the saturated specification 8 is more robust
26:796:69909:15:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:to exclusion of the state level controls. Excluding these controls produces a long run poverty elasticity (standard
26:797:70024:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:error) of -0.397 (0.157) for the saturated model, close to the original elasticity of -0.446 (0.137). In contrast, the
26:798:70142:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:two-way FE estimate is substantially smaller in magnitude when these controls are left out: -0.062(0.087) instead of
26:799:70258:11:10:70:539:82:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:-0.220 (0.084). To the extent unobservables are correlated with observable controls, these results suggests that more
26:800:70375:10:0:72:304:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:saturated specification is better able to account for them.
27:801:70436:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:heterogeneity, as well as its performance on the falsification tests, I use the saturated model to be
27:802:70537:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the preferred specification. At the same time, I recognize that reasonable observers may disagree on
27:803:70637:22:22:71:539:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:which specification is the most reliable, and may place somewhat different weights on the evidence
27:804:70735:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:associated with each specification. For this reason, in this paper I report the range of key estimates
27:805:70837:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:across all eight specifications, which allows readers to put more weight on various specifications
27:806:70935:22:22:72:197:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:based on their own priors.
27:807:70961:22:22:88:539:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:While the specifications in Table 2 include leads and lags in minimum wages, in much of the
27:808:71052:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:literature, estimates come from static models with just a contemporaneous minimum wage. To assess
27:809:71149:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the difference this might make, in Table 7 I report estimates from a static model for the poverty
27:810:71246:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rate. In every set of controls, the minimum wage elasticity from the static model is smaller in
27:811:71341:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:magnitude than either the medium or long run elasticities from the dynamic model. On average, the
27:812:71438:22:22:72:542:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:contemporaneous elasticity from the static model is less than half the size of the long run estimate.
27:813:71539:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:For example, the static two-way fixed effects specification (column 1) that is most commonly used
27:814:71636:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the literature produces an estimate of -0.074, not statistically distinguishable from zero. It also
27:815:71738:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:has a positive leading coefficient of 0.072, although not statistically significant. This subjects the
27:816:71840:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:static elasticity to a positive bias. Indeed, if we estimate a regression with a leading minimum wage
27:817:71941:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in addition to the contemporaneous minimum wage, the magnitude of the minimum wage elasticity
27:818:72034:22:22:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:doubles to -0.144 with a standard error of 0.064, rendering it statistically significant (results not
27:819:72135:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:shown in the table). The addition of lags raise the magnitude further, with the long run estimate
27:820:72232:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:being -0.220. To summarize, the static two-way FE estimate appears to be biased towards zero both
27:821:72329:22:22:72:483:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:due to pre-existing trends, and due to missing some of the lagged effects of the policy.
27:822:72417:22:22:88:541:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:What are the relative contributions of: (1) using a dynamic model, (2) including division-
27:823:72507:22:22:71:539:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:year effects, (3) including Great Recession-state effects, and (4) including state-specific trends in
27:824:72608:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:explaining the gap between the the static, two-way fixed effects estimate (-0.074) and the long
27:825:72703:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:run estimate from the most saturated model (-0.446)? Any decomposition of these four factors
27:826:72795:22:21:71:540:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:will depend on the order in which they are implemented. There are exactly4!  =  24different
27:827:72886:21:22:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:orderings for incrementally changing each of these four factors going from the static version of
27:828:72982:22:22:72:540:117:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:specification 1 to the dynamic version of specification 8, and each of these orderings provides a
27:829:73079:22:22:72:540:95:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:different decomposition. Averaging across these 24 orderings, the average incremental contribution
27:830:73177:22:0:72:540:73:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of these four factors (in the same order as above) are: (1) 44%, (2) 41%, (3) 18%, and (4) -3%. Use
28:831:73278:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the dynamic model (both netting out the lead, and considering long run effects) is the biggest
28:832:73375:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:source of difference, while controls for regional and business cycle heterogeneity are important as
28:833:73474:22:22:71:539:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:well. Use of state-specific trends appears to be the least important of these, at least when considering
28:834:73578:22:46:72:197:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:the poverty rate elasticity.
28:835:73606:46:32:72:170:597:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:4  Discussion
28:836:73619:32:22:71:541:565:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:There is robust evidence that minimum wage increases over the past 30 years have boosted pre-tax-
28:837:73716:22:22:72:540:543:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and-transfer incomes at the bottom of the income distribution. Across specifications with alternative
28:838:73817:22:22:72:540:521:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:assumptions about the appropriate counterfactual, I find that minimum wages reduce the shares
28:839:73910:22:22:71:539:499:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:with family incomes below 50, 75, 100 and 125 percent of the federal poverty threshold. The long run
28:840:74010:22:22:71:541:477:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:poverty rate elasticities range between -0.220 and -0.459, and all of these are statistically significant.
28:841:74116:22:22:72:540:455:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:I also find that a higher minimum wage improves the family income distribution in the sense of
28:842:74210:22:22:72:540:433:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:first order stochastic dominance. The clearest increases are for the 10th and 15th quantiles, with
28:843:74308:22:22:72:540:411:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:elasticities ranging between 0.152 and 0.430 across alternative models. While these results hold
28:844:74404:22:22:72:540:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:across a range of specifications, the preferred specification with a rich set of controls suggest an
28:845:74504:22:22:72:540:367:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:elasticity of around 0.359 for the 10th quantile of family incomes. Overall, around a third of the
28:846:74602:22:22:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income increases resulting from minimum wage changes accrue to those in the bottom 15 percent
28:847:74695:22:21:72:540:323:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the family income distribution (roughly corresponding to those with incomes under the federal
28:848:74791:21:22:72:540:302:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:poverty level), while around 80 percent accrue to those in the bottom third of the family income
28:849:74887:22:22:72:540:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:distribution. At the same time, I also find evidence that there are sizable offsets in public assistance
28:850:74991:22:22:72:540:258:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in response to minimum wage gains. For those in the bottom fifth of the distribution, around 30%
28:851:75087:22:22:72:540:236:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of the income gains are offset through reductions in non-cash-transfers as well as tax credits. These
28:852:75188:22:22:72:540:214:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:offsets seem to be the largest near the federal poverty threshold—consistent with losses in eligibility
28:853:75291:22:22:72:203:192:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in programs such as SNAP.
28:854:75316:22:22:88:539:170:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:What do these estimates imply about the likely impact on poverty from an increase in the
28:855:75404:22:22:72:540:148:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:federal minimum wage from the current $7.25/hour to, say, $12/hour? Taking into account the state
28:856:75501:22:22:72:540:126:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:minimum wages as of January 2017 suggests that this policy would raise the effective minimum
28:857:75593:22:22:71:539:104:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wage—i.e., the maximum of federal or state standard—by 41 percent (or 0.34 log points). Using the
28:858:75690:22:0:71:539:82:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:long run minimum wage elasticity for the poverty rate of -0.446 from the preferred specification and
29:859:75792:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a 12.7 percent poverty rate among the non-elderly population in 2016 suggests a 1.9 percentage
29:860:75886:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:point reduction in the poverty rate from this minimum wage increase. Given the roughly 270 million
29:861:75984:22:22:72:542:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:non-elderly Americans in 2016, this translates into 6.16 million fewer individuals living in poverty.
29:862:76085:22:22:71:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:We can also expect the same minimum wage increase to raise family incomes by 12.2 percent at the
29:863:76181:22:22:71:541:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:10th quantile of the equivalized family income distribution in the long run. For the 10th quantile,
29:864:76280:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:this translates into an annual income increase of $2,140; after accounting for the offset due to
29:865:76376:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:reduced tax credits and transfers, this amounts to an increase of $1,826.22Therefore, the increase
29:866:76474:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in the federal minimum wage can play an important role in reducing poverty and raising family
29:867:76567:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:incomes at the bottom. To put this in context, Hoynes et al. (2006) estimate that EITC reduces
29:868:76661:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:non-elderly poverty rate by around 1.7 percentage points. She also finds that cash transfers (means
29:869:76760:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:tested and non-means tested) cash transfers reduce it by as much as 3.8 percentage point, while
29:870:76855:22:22:72:541:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:non-cash transfers (other than Medicaid) reduce it by around 0.9 percentage point.23In other words,
29:871:76954:22:21:71:539:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a substantial increase in the minimum wage would likely have an impact on the non-elderly poverty
29:872:77051:21:22:72:362:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:rate comparable to means tested public assistance programs.
29:873:77110:22:22:88:539:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The income estimates in this paper do not factor in changes in prices due to minimum wage
29:874:77199:22:22:71:539:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:increase. However, the expected increase in the overall price level from this policy is quite small
29:875:77298:22:22:71:541:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:when compared to the income gains for those at the bottom of the income distribution. For example,
29:876:77396:22:22:71:539:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in a simulation study using input-output tables, MaCurdy (2015) calculated that the bottom quintile
29:877:77495:22:22:71:539:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:faced a 0.5 percent increase in prices from the 21% increase in minimum wage in 1996—an elasticity
29:878:77593:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of around 0.02. The preferred long run elasticity for the 10th quantile after public offsets is around
29:879:77695:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:0.256, or more than an order of magnitude larger. Therefore, netting out the likely price increase
29:880:77793:22:22:71:539:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:would not substantially affect the estimates of the real income gains for the bottom quintile of the
29:881:77893:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:income distribution. However, it does mean that some (possibly much) of these income gains at the
29:882:77990:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:bottom are likely borne by middle and upper income consumers through small increases in prices.
29:883:78085:22:30:88:539:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:The estimates in this paper tend to suggest bigger increases in bottom incomes in response to
29:884:78178:30:15:83:539:152:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:22If we take the range of estimates from all specifications, the proposed minimum wage changes can be expected
29:885:78288:15:11:72:540:137:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:to reduce the poverty rate among the non-elderly population by 0.950 and 1.98 percentage points, hence reducing
29:886:78399:11:11:72:540:126:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the number of non-elderly individuals living in poverty by somewhere between 3.03 and 6.33 million. For the 10th
29:887:78511:11:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:quantile of family incomes, this translates to an annual income increase ranging between 5.2 and 14.5 percent, or
29:888:78624:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:between $905 and $2,937. After accounting for offsets due to lost public assistance, the income increases would range
29:889:78741:11:7:72:175:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:between $657 and $2,790.
29:890:78765:7:14:83:539:86:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:23The estimates for means tested and non-means tested are reported separately in Hoynes et al. (2006); therefore
29:891:78877:14:0:72:395:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the sum of the effects (3.8 percentage point may) may overstate the net impact.
30:892:78958:0:22:72:541:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:minimum wage increases than some simulation based studies such as Sabia and Burkhauser (2010)
30:893:79051:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:or CBO (2014), or MaCurdy (2015). There are a number of problems in using the cross sectional
30:894:79144:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:relationship between reported wages and family incomes to simulate how the gains from a minimum
30:895:79239:22:22:71:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wage increase will be distributed. Most obviously, we would need to make assumptions about how
30:896:79333:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:behavior changes: this includes employer hiring and firing behavior, as well as workers’ job search
30:897:79432:22:22:72:542:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:behavior and labor force participation, which could vary by family income and other characteristics.
30:898:79532:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:In addition, simulations such as these face a number of challenges which tend to suggest a weaker
30:899:79629:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:link between low wages and low family income than is truly the case. A key concern is measurement
30:900:79726:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:error in both wages and other sources of incomes (which includes wage and salary incomes of other
30:901:79823:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:family members). It is a straightforward point that measurement error in reported wages leads to an
30:902:79922:22:22:72:541:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:attenuation in the measured relationship between workers’ wages and family incomes.24As a result,
30:903:80019:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:simulating wage changes for those earning around the minimum wage will typically suggest smaller
30:904:80115:22:21:72:542:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:effects on poverty and smaller income increases at the bottom quantiles than would occur in reality.
30:905:80215:21:22:71:539:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:This is because (1) some of the individuals with high reported wages in low income families are
30:906:80310:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:actually low wage earners, and (2) some of the low wage earners reporting high levels of other sources
30:907:80412:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:of income (including spousal wage and salary income) in reality are in poorer families. A related
30:908:80509:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:practical issue that arises from this is the treatment of sub-minimum wage workers. For example, in
30:909:80608:22:22:72:541:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:their simulations of raising the minimum wage from $5.70 to $7.25, Sabia and Burkhauser (2010)
30:910:80702:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:assume that all those with reported hourly earnings below $5.55 will receive no wage increases
30:911:80796:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:because they are in the “uncovered sector.” Moreover, they assume that no one above $7.25 will
30:912:80890:22:22:72:542:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:get a raise. These particular assumptions seem implausible due to both measurement error issues,
30:913:80986:22:22:72:542:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:as well as the well known “lighthouse effect” phenomenon whereby even uncovered sector workers’
30:914:81081:22:17:71:539:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:wages are affected by minimum wages (Card and Krueger 1995; Boeri et al. 2011). Moreover, as
30:915:81173:17:15:83:540:209:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:24Consider the relationship between own wage income,W, and family incomeF=W+I, whereIrepresents other
30:916:81274:15:12:72:540:194:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:incomes (possibly others’ wages). The linear approximation to the true relationship is represented by the population
30:917:81390:12:14:72:540:182:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:regressionF=βW+u. Note thatβ=Cov(W+I,W)V(W)= 1 +σWIσ2W. So if wages are at all positively correlated with other
30:918:81501:14:11:72:283:168:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:sources of family incomes,I, as is likely, thenβ >1.
30:919:81553:11:11:81:540:157:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:Now consider the case whereWis measured with error, so that ̃W=W+e, and ̃F=W+I+eare the observed
30:920:81649:11:11:71:539:146:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:wage and family income. This is slightly different from the textbook classical measurement error case because the
30:921:81762:11:11:72:539:135:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:measurement error,e, affects both the independent and dependent variables. Substituting the reported values into the
30:922:81878:11:12:72:508:124:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:true regression equation produces ̃F−e=β( ̃W−e). Rearranging, we have ̃F=β ̃W+ (1−β)e=β ̃W+  ̃u.
30:923:81974:12:17:81:539:112:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f18:Note that ̃β=Cov( ̃F, ̃W)V( ̃W)is the estimate from a population regression of ̃Fon ̃W. Substituting ̃F=β ̃W+(1−β)e
30:924:82089:17:0:72:294:95:9:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f12:into the expression for ̃βwe have ̃β=β+ (1−β)σ
30:925:82135:0:11:295:297:102:5:g_d0_f22:5:g_d0_f21:2e
30:926:82137:11:9:282:539:91:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f7:σ2w+σ2e,which will be attenuated towards zero ifβ >1, which
30:927:82196:9:10:71:539:82:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:is true if wages are at all positively correlated with other sources of family incomes. The attenuation will also be
30:928:82312:10:0:72:331:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:proportionate to the share of wage variance that is due to error.
31:929:82379:0:22:71:539:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Autor et al. (2016) show, effects of the minimum wage extend up to the 20th percentile of the wage
31:930:82477:22:22:72:539:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:distribution, which would be unlikely absent some spillovers.25Therefore, results from simulation
31:931:82574:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:studies may not provide reliable guidance in assessing the impact of minimum wages on bottom
31:932:82666:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:incomes, making it critical for us to consider actual evidence from past minimum wage changes
31:933:82759:22:22:71:228:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:when analyzing policy proposals.
31:934:82791:22:22:88:539:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:While minimum wages tend to raise family incomes at the bottom, they also tend to substitute
31:935:82883:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:earnings for public assistance. Were we to assess public policies strictly based on their efficacy
31:936:82981:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:in reducing post-tax and transfer poverty, the offsets through reduced tax credits and non-cash
31:937:83076:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:transfers further suggests a lower effectiveness of minimum wages in raising post-tax-and-transfer
31:938:83174:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:incomes. Policies like cash transfers, SNAP, and tax credits are better targeted to raise incomes for
31:939:83275:22:22:72:322:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:those at the very bottom of the income distribution.
31:940:83327:22:22:88:539:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:At the same time, there are positive aspects of a policy that reduces public assistance via
31:941:83418:22:21:71:541:445:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:increased earnings. First, a reduction in public benefits like SNAP can be efficiency enhancing,
31:942:83514:21:22:71:541:424:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:since in principle these programs are funded using taxation which can have deadweight losses.
31:943:83607:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Hendren (2014) finds that that lower pre-tax incomes at the bottom has an efficiency cost due to
31:944:83703:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:such transfers: a $1 of surplus accruing to the bottom quintile of the income distribution can be
31:945:83800:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:transformed into a $1.15 surplus for everyone. A corollary to that argument is that by reducing
31:946:83895:22:22:72:539:336:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:such transfers, minimum wages can have an efficiency-enhancing attribute.26Alternatively, if there
31:947:83993:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:are deadweight losses from the minimum wage policy, the reduced public assistance will tend to
31:948:84087:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:mitigate such distortions. Additionally, there is increasing recognition that individuals may not see
31:949:84188:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:labor earnings and tax credits/transfers as perfect substitutes, and may prefer to receive a higher
31:950:84287:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:compensation for their work than what is often perceived as a government transfer. Relatedly, voters
31:951:84387:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:may prefer “pre-distributive” policies like minimum wages over “re-distributive” ones using tax and
31:952:84486:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:transfers even when they are concerned with inequality—in part because of low levels of trust in
31:953:84582:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:government (Kuziemko et al. (2015)). All of these factors add to the cost of pre-tax inequality
31:954:84677:22:19:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:and raises the benefits of a policy like minimum wage that affects the pre-tax-and-transfer income
31:955:84775:19:15:83:540:141:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:25Autor, Manning and Smith also highlight how measurement error in wages and wage spillovers have similar
31:956:84880:15:11:72:540:126:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:implications about the effects of minimum on the observed wage distribution. This is an interesting point which affects
31:957:84999:11:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the interpretation of the effects on higher wage quantiles. But for our purposes here, regardless of the interpretation of
31:958:85121:11:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:these effects as true spillovers or measurement error spillovers, ignoring them will tend to downward bias the predicted
31:959:85241:11:7:72:310:93:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:effects of minimum wages on poverty in simulation studies.
31:960:85299:7:14:83:541:86:6:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f7:26Moreover, the public savings afforded by a higher minimum wage could be used to expand program generosity,
31:961:85407:14:0:72:237:72:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:further enhancing income at the bottom.
32:962:85448:0:22:72:131:709:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:distribution.
32:963:85461:22:22:88:539:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Overall, motivations of voters and policy makers in raising minimum wage policies tend to
32:964:85550:22:22:71:539:665:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:go beyond reducing poverty. For example, using data from the 2016 YouGov Common Content
32:965:85637:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:Pre-Election Survey of voters (N=1,000), I find that voters’ preferred level of federal minimum wage
32:966:85737:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:barely changes (from $10.45 to $10.18) if there were also to be sufficient tax credits to eliminate
32:967:85836:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:poverty among working families. (See Online Appendix Figure B.4.) This is consistent with the
32:968:85929:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:observation that the popular support for minimum wages is in part fueled by a desire to raise
32:969:86022:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:earnings of low and moderate income families more broadly, and by concerns of fairness that seek to
32:970:86121:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:limit the extent of wage inequality (Green and Harrison, 2010), or employers’ exercise of market
32:971:86217:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:power (Fehr and Fischbacher 2004; Kahneman et al. 1986). The findings from this paper suggest
32:972:86310:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:that attaining these goals is also consistent with at least a moderate increase in family incomes, and
32:973:86412:22:0:72:503:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:a reduced reliance on public assistance for those at the bottom of the income distribution.
